<p><i><b>Toy Story 3</b></i> is a 2010 American <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a> <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">computer-animated</a> <a href="/wiki/Comedy_film" title="Comedy film">comedy film</a>, and the third film in the <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_(franchise)" title="Toy Story (franchise)">Toy Story</a></i> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nola-t3_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-nola-t3-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> It was produced by <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar Animation Studios</a> and released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>. Directed by <a href="/wiki/Lee_Unkrich" title="Lee Unkrich">Lee Unkrich</a>, the screenplay was written by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Arndt" title="Michael Arndt">Michael Arndt</a>, while Unkrich wrote the story along with <a href="/wiki/John_Lasseter" title="John Lasseter">John Lasseter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Stanton" title="Andrew Stanton">Andrew Stanton</a>, respectively director and co-writer of the first two films. The film was released worldwide from June through October<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Digital_3-D" title="Disney Digital 3-D">Disney Digital 3-D</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RealD_Cinema" title="RealD Cinema">RealD</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMAX_3D" title="IMAX 3D">IMAX 3D</a> formats. <i>Toy Story 3</i> was the first film to be released theatrically with <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Surround_7.1" title="Dolby Surround 7.1">Dolby Surround 7.1</a> sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-market_watch_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-market_watch-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The plot focuses on the toys <a href="/wiki/Sheriff_Woody" title="Sheriff Woody">Woody</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Lightyear" title="Buzz Lightyear">Buzz Lightyear</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Toy_Story_characters#Andy.27s_toys" title="List of Toy Story characters">their friends</a> dealing with an uncertain future as their owner, Andy, prepares to leave for college. Actors <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Allen" title="Tim Allen">Tim Allen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Cusack" title="Joan Cusack">Joan Cusack</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Morris_(actor)" title="John Morris (actor)">John Morris</a>, along with few others reprised their voice-over roles from the previous films.</p>
<p>The film received widespread critical acclaim earning a 99% 'certified fresh' rating at <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rt_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-rt-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> and a score of 92 at <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>. The feature broke <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_the_Third" title="Shrek the Third">Shrek the Third</a></i> '​s record as the biggest opening day North American gross for an animated film unadjusted for inflation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> and had a big opening weekend with an unadjusted gross of $110,307,189. It is also the highest-grossing opening weekend for a Pixar film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> and was previously the highest-grossing opening weekend for a film to have opened in the month of June (surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manofsteel_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-manofsteel-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-openingjune_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-openingjune-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> This is the <a href="/wiki/2010_in_film" title="2010 in film">highest-grossing film of 2010</a>, both in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">United States and Canada</a>, and worldwide. In early August, it became Pixar's highest-grossing film at the North American and worldwide box offices (surpassing <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i>), and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_animated_films" title="List of highest-grossing animated films">highest-grossing animated film of all time</a> worldwide (surpassing <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_2" title="Shrek 2">Shrek 2</a>)</i> until it was surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Frozen_(2013_film)" title="Frozen (2013 film)"><i>Frozen</i></a> in March 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWHighestGross_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-EWHighestGross-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TimeFrozenTop_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-TimeFrozenTop-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Toy Story 3</i> became the first animated film in history to make over $1 billion worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onebill_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-onebill-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">13th-highest-grossing film of all time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo-alltime_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-alltime-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Toy Story 3</i> was nominated for five <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Adapted_Screenplay" title="Academy Award for Best Adapted Screenplay">Best Adapted Screenplay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Editing">Best Sound Editing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oscar_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-oscar-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> It was the third animated film (after <i><a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_(1991_film)" title="Beauty and the Beast (1991 film)">Beauty and the Beast</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Up_(2009_film)" title="Up (2009 film)">Up</a></i>) to be nominated for Academy Award for Best Picture. It won the awards for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Animated_Feature" title="Academy Award for Best Animated Feature">Best Animated Feature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oscar_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-oscar-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> A sequel, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toy_Story_4" title="Toy Story 4">Toy Story 4</a></i>, directed by Lasseter and with a story by Unkrich, Stanton, and <a href="/wiki/Pete_Docter" title="Pete Docter">Pete Docter</a>, is planned for a 2017 release.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andy_Davis_(Toy_Story)" title="Andy Davis (Toy Story)">Andy</a>, now 17 years old,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> is about to leave for college, and his toys have not been played with for years. He intends to take only <a href="/wiki/Sheriff_Woody" title="Sheriff Woody">Woody</a> with him to college, and puts <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Lightyear" title="Buzz Lightyear">Buzz Lightyear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessie_(Toy_Story)" title="Jessie (Toy Story)">Jessie</a> and the other toys in a bag to be stored in the attic. Andy's mother mistakenly takes the bag to the curb for garbage pickup. The toys escape and, believing Andy intended to throw them away, decide to climb in a donation box with <a href="/wiki/List_of_Toy_Story_characters#Barbie" title="List of Toy Story characters">Barbie</a> bound for Sunnyside Daycare. Woody follows them and tries to explain the mistake, but they refuse to believe him.</p>
<p>Andy's toys are welcomed by the other toys at Sunnyside, and are given a tour of the seemingly perfect play-setting by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lots-O%27-Huggin%27_Bear" title="Lots-O'-Huggin' Bear">Lots-O'-Huggin' Bear</a> (simply known as Lotso), <a href="/wiki/List_of_Toy_Story_characters#Big_Baby" title="List of Toy Story characters">Big Baby</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Toy_Story_characters#Ken" title="List of Toy Story characters">Ken</a>, with whom Barbie falls in love. All of the toys choose to stay, except Woody, who attempts to return to Andy. Woody is found by Bonnie, one of the Sunnyside students. She takes Woody home and plays with him along with her other toys, which are well-treated. At Sunnyside, a group of toddlers play rough with Andy's toys.</p>
<p>Buzz asks Lotso to have them moved to the older children's room, but is captured. Lotso, who controls Sunnyside ruthlessly at night when the teachers and students are not around, reveals he sends new toys to distract the toddlers to keep him and his henchmen safe, not caring whether the toys are broken in the process. Seeing promise in Buzz, he resets him to his original space ranger persona, resetting his memory. At the same time, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mrs._Potato_Head_(Toy_Story)" title="Mrs. Potato Head (Toy Story)">Mrs. Potato Head</a> (who accidentally left one of her eyes at Andy's house) sees Andy searching for the toys and convinces the toys that Woody told the truth. But before they can leave, Andy's toys are imprisoned by Lotso's gang.</p>
<p>At Bonnie's house, before Woody leaves to find Andy, he learns from a toy clown named <a href="/wiki/List_of_Toy_Story_characters#Chuckles" title="List of Toy Story characters">Chuckles</a> that he, Lotso and Big Baby once had a beloved owner named Daisy. When the toys were accidentally left behind by Daisy's family during a trip, they eventually returned to her house, only to find that Lotso had been replaced with a similar toy, causing Lotso to become embittered.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toy_Story_3_incinerator_scene_screenshot.jpg"><img alt="The scene with woody close to the incinerator" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="800" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Toy_Story_3_incinerator_scene_screenshot.jpg/325px-Toy_Story_3_incinerator_scene_screenshot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Toy_Story_3_incinerator_scene_screenshot.jpg/488px-Toy_Story_3_incinerator_scene_screenshot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Toy_Story_3_incinerator_scene_screenshot.jpg/650px-Toy_Story_3_incinerator_scene_screenshot.jpg 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toy_Story_3_incinerator_scene_screenshot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The scene with Woody close to the incinerator. This sequence in the furnace required the combined efforts of special effects, photography and music to emphasize the drama of the scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Woody returns to Sunnyside and reconciles with Andy's other toys. That night, the toys attempt to escape, and accidentally reset Buzz to Spanish mode instead of his original persona. Buzz allies himself with Woody and falls in love with Jessie. The toys reach a dumpster, but are caught by Lotso and his gang. As a garbage truck approaches, Woody reveals what he learned about Lotso. Lotso says that he now thinks toys are meant to be discarded, leading an enraged Big Baby to throw Lotso into the dumpster. As the toys try to run away, Lotso pulls Woody into the dumpster just as the truck collects the trash. Woody's friends fall into the back of the truck while trying to rescue him, and a falling television lands on Buzz, restoring his memory and normal persona.</p>
<p>The truck deposits the toys at the tri-county landfill, where they find themselves on a conveyor belt leading to an incinerator. Woody and Buzz help Lotso reach an emergency stop button, only for Lotso to abandon them. Thinking that the end is near, the toys accept their fate, but are rescued by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squeeze_Toy_Aliens" title="Squeeze Toy Aliens">Aliens</a> operating an industrial claw. Lotso escapes, but a garbage truck driver finds him and straps him to his truck's radiator <a href="/wiki/Grille_(motor_vehicle)" title="Grille (motor vehicle)">grill</a>. Woody and his friends board another garbage truck, driven by a now adult <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sid_(Toy_Story)" title="Sid (Toy Story)">Sid Phillips</a>, back to Andy's house.</p>
<p>In Andy's room, Woody climbs into the box with Andy's college supplies, while the other toys ready themselves for the attic. Woody leaves a note for Andy, who, thinking the note is from his mother, takes the toys to Bonnie's house and introduces her to them. Bonnie recognizes Woody, who, to Andy's surprise, is at the bottom of the box. Though hesitant at first, Andy passes him on to Bonnie, and then plays with her before leaving. Woody and the other toys watch Andy's departure before beginning their new lives with Bonnie.</p>
<p>During the credits, Woody and the other toys learn that Barbie, Ken and Big Baby have improved the lives of the toys at Sunnyside.</p>

<p>Several other characters (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bo_Peep_(Toy_Story)" title="Bo Peep (Toy Story)">Bo Peep</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RC_(Toy_Story)" title="RC (Toy Story)">RC</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Toy_Story_characters#Etch" title="List of Toy Story characters">Etch</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wheezy" title="Wheezy">Wheezy</a>) are only seen in flashbacks or briefly mentioned. The character of Slinky Dog appeared to be in limbo after the death of his original voice actor <a href="/wiki/Jim_Varney" title="Jim Varney">Jim Varney</a> on February 10, 2000, three months after <i>Toy Story 2</i> was released. Varney was replaced by Blake Clark. After Clark was cast to play Slinky Dog, the producers realized that Clark and Varney had coincidentally been close friends since they appeared in the 1989 film <i><a href="/wiki/Fast_Food_(film)" title="Fast Food (film)">Fast Food</a></i>, making the transition a lot easier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the terms of Pixar's initial seven-film deal with <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">Disney</a>, all characters created by Pixar for their films were owned by Disney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBSNewsAdios_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBSNewsAdios-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Furthermore, Disney retained the rights to make sequels to any Pixar film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBSNewsAdios_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-CBSNewsAdios-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> though Pixar retained the <a href="/wiki/Right_of_first_refusal" title="Right of first refusal">right of first refusal</a> to work on these sequels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, when the contentious negotiations between the two companies made a split appear likely, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Eisner" title="Michael Eisner">Michael Eisner</a>, Disney chairman at the time, put plans in motion to produce <i>Toy Story 3</i> at a new Disney studio, <a href="/wiki/Circle_7_Animation" title="Circle 7 Animation">Circle 7 Animation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-untold_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-untold-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Tim Allen, the voice of Buzz Lightyear, indicated a willingness to return, even if Pixar was not on board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-untold_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-untold-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:2</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ToyStory3PromoImage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="267" data-file-width="400" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/ToyStory3PromoImage.jpg/240px-ToyStory3PromoImage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/ToyStory3PromoImage.jpg/360px-ToyStory3PromoImage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/54/ToyStory3PromoImage.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ToyStory3PromoImage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Promotional art for <a href="/wiki/Circle_7_Animation" title="Circle 7 Animation">Circle 7</a>'s <i>Toy Story 3</i>, displaying the storyline of the <a href="/wiki/Product_recall" title="Product recall">recalled</a> Buzz Lightyears.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Jim_Herzfeld" title="Jim Herzfeld">Jim Herzfeld</a> wrote a script for Circle 7's version of the film. It focused on the other toys shipping a malfunctioning Buzz to <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, where he was built, believing that he will be fixed there. While searching on the Internet, they find out that many more Buzz Lightyear toys are malfunctioning around the world and the company has issued a massive <a href="/wiki/Product_recall" title="Product recall">recall</a>. Fearing Buzz's destruction, a group of Andy's toys (Woody, Rex, Slinky, Mr. Potato Head, Hamm, Jessie, and Bullseye) venture out to rescue Buzz. At the same time, Buzz meets other toys from around the world that were once loved, but have now been recalled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-untold_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-untold-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2006, <a href="/wiki/Pixar#Disney" title="Pixar">Disney bought Pixar</a> in a deal that put Pixar chiefs <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Catmull" title="Edwin Catmull">Edwin Catmull</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Lasseter" title="John Lasseter">John Lasseter</a> in charge of all Disney Animation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Shortly thereafter, Circle 7 Animation was shut down and its version of <i>Toy Story 3</i> was cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-untold_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-untold-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:1</sup> The character designs went into the Disney archives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The following month, Disney CEO <a href="/wiki/Bob_Iger" title="Bob Iger">Robert Iger</a> confirmed that Disney was in the process of transferring the production to Pixar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> John Lasseter, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Stanton" title="Andrew Stanton">Andrew Stanton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Docter" title="Pete Docter">Pete Docter</a>, and Lee Unkrich visited the house where they first pitched <i>Toy Story</i> and came up with the story for the film over a weekend. Stanton then wrote a <a href="/wiki/Film_treatment" title="Film treatment">treatment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pr_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-pr-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> On February 8, 2007, Catmull announced <i>Toy Story 2</i> '​s co-director, Lee Unkrich, as the sole director of the film instead of John Lasseter (who was busy directing <i><a href="/wiki/Cars_2" title="Cars 2">Cars 2</a></i>), and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Arndt" title="Michael Arndt">Michael Arndt</a> as screenwriter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The release date was moved to 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Unkrich said that he felt pressure to avoid creating "the first dud" for Pixar, since (as of 2010) all of Pixar's films had been critical and commercial successes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lee_Unkrich_at_WonderCon_2010_3.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Lee_Unkrich_at_WonderCon_2010_3.JPG/220px-Lee_Unkrich_at_WonderCon_2010_3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Lee_Unkrich_at_WonderCon_2010_3.JPG/330px-Lee_Unkrich_at_WonderCon_2010_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Lee_Unkrich_at_WonderCon_2010_3.JPG/440px-Lee_Unkrich_at_WonderCon_2010_3.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lee_Unkrich_at_WonderCon_2010_3.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lee_Unkrich" title="Lee Unkrich">Lee Unkrich</a>, pictured at the <i>Toy Story 3</i> panel at WonderCon 2010 in April 2010, was the full-time director for the film.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the initial development stages of the film, Pixar revisited their work from the original <i>Toy Story</i> and found that, although they could open the old <a href="/wiki/Computer_file" title="Computer file">computer files</a> for the animated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3D_model" title="3D model">3D models</a>, error messages prevented them from editing the files. This necessitated recreating the models from scratch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> To create the chaotic and complex junkyard scene near the film's end, more than a year and a half was invested on research and development to create the simulation systems required for the sequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Instead of sending Tom Hanks, Tim Allen and John Ratzenberger scripts for their consideration in reprising their roles, a complete story reel of the film was shown to the actors in a theater. The reel was made up of moving storyboards with pre-recorded voices, sound effects, and music. At the conclusion of the preview, the actors signed on to the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_online_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-empire_online-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dolby_Laboratories" title="Dolby Laboratories">Dolby Laboratories</a> announced that <i>Toy Story 3</i> would be the first film that will feature theatrical <a href="/wiki/7.1_surround_sound" title="7.1 surround sound">7.1 surround sound</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-market_watch_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-market_watch-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Thus, even the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> version will feature original 7.1 audio, unlike other films which were remixed into 7.1 for Blu-ray.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toy_Story_3,_El_Capitan_Theatre,_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="3570" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Toy_Story_3%2C_El_Capitan_Theatre%2C_2010.jpg/220px-Toy_Story_3%2C_El_Capitan_Theatre%2C_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Toy_Story_3%2C_El_Capitan_Theatre%2C_2010.jpg/330px-Toy_Story_3%2C_El_Capitan_Theatre%2C_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Toy_Story_3%2C_El_Capitan_Theatre%2C_2010.jpg/440px-Toy_Story_3%2C_El_Capitan_Theatre%2C_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toy_Story_3,_El_Capitan_Theatre,_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Toy Story 3</i> had its United States premiere at <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReutersPremiere_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersPremiere-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> which also hosted a <i>Toy Story</i> marathon showing for the first time all three films together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BWTakesOver_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-BWTakesOver-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Toy Story 3</i> had its world-wide premiere on June 12, 2010, opening at <a href="/wiki/Taormina_Film_Fest" title="Taormina Film Fest">Taormina Film Fest</a> in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United States, it premiered on June 13, 2010 at <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a> in Hollywood, California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReutersPremiere_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersPremiere-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> El Capitan also hosted on June 17, 2010 a <i>Toy Story</i> marathon, showing for the first time all three <i>Toy Story</i> films together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BWTakesOver_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-BWTakesOver-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The film went into its wide release on June 18, 2010, along with a release to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMAX_3D" title="IMAX 3D">IMAX 3D</a> theaters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film was theatrically accompanied with the Pixar short film <i><a href="/wiki/Day_%26_Night_(2010_film)" title="Day &amp; Night (2010 film)">Day &amp; Night</a></i>, which focuses on what happens when an animated personification of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daytime_(astronomy)" title="Daytime (astronomy)">Day</a> meets his opposite, Night, and the resulting growth for both.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film's first <a href="/wiki/Teaser_campaign" title="Teaser campaign">teaser trailer</a> was released with <i><a href="/wiki/Up_(2009_film)" title="Up (2009 film)">Up</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Disney_Digital_3-D" title="Disney Digital 3-D">Disney Digital 3-D</a>, on May 29, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 2, 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story" title="Toy Story">Toy Story</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_2" title="Toy Story 2">Toy Story 2</a></i> were re-released as a double feature in Disney Digital 3-D.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-releasedate_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-releasedate-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The first full-length <a href="/wiki/Trailer_(promotion)" title="Trailer (promotion)">trailer</a> was attached as an exclusive sneak peek and a first footage to the <i>Toy Story</i> double feature, on October 12, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> A second teaser was released on February 10, 2010, followed by a second full-length trailer on February 11, and appeared in 3D showings of <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/How_to_Train_Your_Dragon_(film)" title="How to Train Your Dragon (film)">How to Train Your Dragon</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> On March 23, 2010, <i>Toy Story</i> was released on Blu-ray/DVD combo pack, which included a small feature of "The Story of <i>Toy Story 3</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, <i>Toy Story 2</i> was released on the same day in the same format, which had a small feature on the "Characters of <i>Toy Story 3</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joan_Cusack_June_2010_Toy_Story.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Joan_Cusack_June_2010_Toy_Story.jpg/220px-Joan_Cusack_June_2010_Toy_Story.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Joan_Cusack_June_2010_Toy_Story.jpg/330px-Joan_Cusack_June_2010_Toy_Story.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Joan_Cusack_June_2010_Toy_Story.jpg/440px-Joan_Cusack_June_2010_Toy_Story.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joan_Cusack_June_2010_Toy_Story.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Joan_Cusack" title="Joan Cusack">Joan Cusack</a>, who voiced Jessie in the film, signing <i>Toy Story 3</i> merchandise.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mattel" title="Mattel">Mattel</a>, Thinkway Toys, and <a href="/wiki/Lego_Toy_Story" title="Lego Toy Story">Lego</a> are among companies who produced toys to promote the film. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fisher_Price" title="Fisher Price">Fisher Price</a>, a Mattel Company, has released <i>Toy Story 3</i> with twenty-one 3D images for viewing with the <a href="/wiki/View-Master" title="View-Master">View-Master</a> viewer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Disney_Interactive_Studios" title="Disney Interactive Studios">Disney Interactive Studios</a> also produced a video game based on the film, <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_3:_The_Video_Game" title="Toy Story 3: The Video Game">Toy Story 3: The Video Game</a></i>, which was released for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PSP" title="PSP">PSP</a> on June 15, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> version was released on October 30, 2010, as part of a PS2 bundle and separately on November 2, 2010 (the same day <i>Toy Story 3</i> was released on DVD and Blu-ray).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amazon1_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-amazon1-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also the last Disney/Pixar game to be released on PlayStation 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amazon1_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-amazon1-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Toy Story 3</i> was featured in Apple's iPhone <a href="/wiki/IOS_4" title="IOS 4">OS 4</a> Event on April 8, 2010, with <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> demonstrating a <i>Toy Story 3</i> themed <a href="/wiki/IAd" title="IAd">iAd</a> written in <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Pixar designed a commercial for the toy, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lots-O%27-Huggin%27_Bear#Lots-O.27-Huggin.27_Bear" title="Lots-O'-Huggin' Bear">Lots-O'-Huggin' Bear</a>, and formatted it to appear as if it came from an old VCR recording. The recording was altered with distorted sound, noise along the bottom of the screen, and flickering video, all designed to make it look like a converted recording from around 1983.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> A Japanese version of the commercial was also released online, with the name "Lots-O'-Huggin Bear" replaced with "Little Hug-Hug Bear" (Japanese:ハグハグベアちゃん/<i>Hagu Hagu Beya-Chan</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._season_10)" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. season 10)">Dancing with the Stars</a></i> '​ May 11, 2010, episode, the <a href="/wiki/Gipsy_Kings" title="Gipsy Kings">Gipsy Kings</a> performed a Spanish-language version of the song "<a href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_a_Friend_in_Me" title="You've Got a Friend in Me">You've Got a Friend in Me</a>," which featured a <a href="/wiki/Pasodoble" title="Pasodoble">paso doble</a> dance choreographed by <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_Burke" title="Cheryl Burke">Cheryl Burke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Dovolani" title="Tony Dovolani">Tony Dovolani</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Both the song and dance are featured in the film. <i>Toy Story 3</i> was promoted with airings of the first and second film on several channels in the weeks preceding the film's release, including <a href="/wiki/Disney_Channel" title="Disney Channel">Disney Channel</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Disney_XD" title="Disney XD">Disney XD</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/ABC_Family" title="ABC Family">ABC Family</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WrapABCFirstLook_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-WrapABCFirstLook-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Sneak peeks of <i>Toy Story 3</i> were also revealed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WrapABCFirstLook_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-WrapABCFirstLook-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> primarily on Disney Channel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Oscar_campaign">Oscar campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Oscar campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Toy Story 3</i> '​s "Not since..." Oscar campaign drew a lot of attention, emphasizing the film's uniqueness and critical acclaim. The campaign consisted of posters featuring characters from the film, comparing <i>Toy Story 3</i> to previous winners such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Shakespeare_in_Love" title="Shakespeare in Love">Shakespeare in Love</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> and more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Walt Disney Studios Chairman Rich Ross explained they were going for the Best Picture win, not just Best Animated film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> The Hollywood Reporter gave the campaign a bronze award in Key Art Awards Winners 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Toy Story 3</i> was released in North America on November 2, 2010, in a standard DVD edition, two-disc Blu-ray, and in a four-disc Blu-ray/DVD/Digital Copy combo pack. Features include behind the scenes, including a sneak peek teaser for the upcoming <i>Cars 2</i>, the sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Cars_(film)" title="Cars (film)">Cars</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> A 10-disc <i>Toy Story</i> trilogy Blu-ray box set arrived on store shelves on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/List_of_Blu-ray_3D_releases" title="List of Blu-ray 3D releases">3D</a> version of the Blu-ray was released in North America on November 1, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On its first week of release (November 2–7, 2010) it sold 3,859,736 units (equal to $73,096,452), ranking No.1 for the week and immediately becoming the best-selling animated film of 2010 in units sold (surpassing <i>How to Train Your Dragon</i>). As of July 18, 2012, it has sold 10,911,701 units ($185,924,247).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> It has become the best-selling DVD of 2010 in units sold, but it lacks in sales revenue and, therefore, ranks second behind <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)#Home_media" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i> on that list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> It also sold about 4.0 million Blu-ray units, ranking as the fourth best-selling film of 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the U.K., it broke the record for the largest first day ever for animated feature, both on DVD and Blu-ray, in sales revenue. Additionally, on its first day of release on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>, it immediately became the most downloaded Disney film ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="Critics"></span><span id="Critical_reception"></span> <i>Toy Story 3</i> received widespread acclaim from critics. Review aggregation website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> gives the film a score of 99% based on reviews from 279 critics, with an average score of 8.9/10. The site's consensus was, "Deftly blending comedy, adventure, and honest emotion, <i>Toy Story 3</i> is a rare second sequel that really works."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rt_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-rt-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Toy Story 3 was the best-reviewed film of 2010 on Rotten Tomatoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Another review aggregator, <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Normalization_(statistics)" title="Normalization (statistics)">normalized</a> rating out of 100 top reviews from mainstream critics, calculated a score of 92 based on 39 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">TIME</a></i> named <i>Toy Story 3</i> the best film of 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> as did <a href="/wiki/Quentin_Tarantino" title="Quentin Tarantino">Quentin Tarantino</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nordyke1_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-nordyke1-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, <i>TIME</i> named it one of "The 25 All-TIME Best Animated Films."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Audiences surveyed by Cinemascore gave the film a grade A rating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quentin_Tarantino_C%C3%A9sars_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="509" data-file-width="472" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Quentin_Tarantino_C%C3%A9sars_2011.jpg/220px-Quentin_Tarantino_C%C3%A9sars_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Quentin_Tarantino_C%C3%A9sars_2011.jpg/330px-Quentin_Tarantino_C%C3%A9sars_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Quentin_Tarantino_C%C3%A9sars_2011.jpg/440px-Quentin_Tarantino_C%C3%A9sars_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quentin_Tarantino_C%C3%A9sars_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Quentin_Tarantino" title="Quentin Tarantino">Quentin Tarantino</a> placed the film at the top position in his list of favorite films of 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nordyke1_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-nordyke1-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> stated, "This film—this whole three-part, 15-year epic—about the adventures of a bunch of silly plastic junk turns out also to be a long, melancholy meditation on loss, impermanence and that noble, stubborn, foolish thing called love."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Owen_Gleiberman" title="Owen Gleiberman">Owen Gleiberman</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> gave the film an A, saying, "Even with the bar raised high, <i>Toy Story 3</i> enchanted and moved me so deeply I was flabbergasted that a digitally animated comedy about plastic playthings could have this effect."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Gleiberman also wrote in the next issue that he, along with many other grown men, cried at the end of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Michael Rechtshaffen of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> also gave the film a positive review, saying, "Woody, Buzz and playmates make a thoroughly engaging, emotionally satisfying return."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mark_Kermode" title="Mark Kermode">Mark Kermode</a> of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> gave the film, and the series, a glowing review, calling it "the best movie trilogy of all time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, Claudia Puig gave the film a complete 4 <a href="/wiki/Star_(classification)" title="Star (classification)">star rating</a>, writing, "This installment, the best of the three, is everything a movie should be: hilarious, touching, exciting and clever."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lou_Lumenick" title="Lou Lumenick">Lou Lumenick</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i> wrote, "<i>Toy Story 3</i> (which is pointlessly being shown in 3-D at most locations) may not be a masterpiece, but it still had me in tears at the end."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Phillips_(critic)" title="Michael Phillips (critic)">Michael Phillips</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> gave the film 3 out of 4 stars, writing that, "Compared with the riches of all kinds in recent Pixar masterworks such as <i><a href="/wiki/Ratatouille_(film)" title="Ratatouille (film)">Ratatouille</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/WALL-E" title="WALL-E">WALL-E</a></i>, and <i>Up</i>, <i>Toy Story 3</i> looks and plays like an exceptionally slick and confident product, as opposed to a magical blend of commerce and popular art."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Orlando_Sentinel" title="Orlando Sentinel">Orlando Sentinel</a></i> film critic Roger Moore, who gave the film 3½ out of 4 stars, wrote, "Dazzling, scary and sentimental, <i>Toy Story 3</i> is a dark and emotional conclusion to the film series that made Pixar famous."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide">Worldwide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Worldwide">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Toy Story 3</i> earned $415,004,880 in North America, and $648,167,031 in other countries, totaling $1,063,171,911 worldwide, earning more revenue than the previous two films of the series combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo1_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-mojo1-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> It became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_animated_films#Highest-grossing_animated_films" title="List of highest-grossing animated films">highest-grossing animated film</a>, surpassing six-year-old record held by <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_2" title="Shrek 2">Shrek 2</a></i> ($919 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWHighestGross_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-EWHighestGross-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> until <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios" title="Walt Disney Animation Studios">Walt Disney Animation Studios</a>' film <i><a href="/wiki/Frozen_(2013_film)" title="Frozen (2013 film)">Frozen</a></i> surpassed it in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TimeFrozenTop_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-TimeFrozenTop-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films#Highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">thirteenth highest-grossing film</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo-alltime_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-alltime-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing <a href="/wiki/2010_in_film" title="2010 in film">2010 film</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> the second highest-grossing animated film (behind <a href="/wiki/Frozen_(2013_film)" title="Frozen (2013 film)"><i>Frozen</i></a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onebill_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-onebill-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing film in the <a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_(franchise)" title="Toy Story (franchise)"><i>Toy Story</i></a> series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> the fifth highest-grossing Disney film<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> and the highest-grossing Pixar film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pixar_Movies_at_the_Box_Office_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pixar_Movies_at_the_Box_Office-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In estimated attendance, though, it still ranks fourth on the list of modern animated films, behind <i>Shrek 2</i>, <i>Finding Nemo</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onebill_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-onebill-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> On its first weekend, <i>Toy Story 3</i> topped the worldwide box office with $145.3 million ($153.7 million with weekday previews), the third-largest opening weekend worldwide for an animated feature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 27, 2010, its 73rd day of release, it surpassed the $1 billion mark, becoming the third Disney film, the second Disney film in 2010 (after <i>Alice in Wonderland</i>) and the first animated film to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onebill_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-onebill-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In North America, <i>Toy Story 3</i> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">twelfth highest-grossing film</a>, unadjusted for inflation. Adjusted for ticket price inflation though, it ranks 90th on the all-time chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> It is also the highest-grossing 2010 film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing Pixar film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pixar_Movies_at_the_Box_Office_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pixar_Movies_at_the_Box_Office-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> the second-highest-grossing G-rated film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> the third-highest-grossing animated film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> and the fourth-highest-grossing film distributed by Disney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The film earned $41,148,961 on its opening day (Friday, June 18, 2010) from 4,028 theaters, including $4 million at midnight shows from about 1,500 theaters, setting an opening-day record for an animated film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During its opening weekend, the film topped the box office with $110,307,189, setting an opening-weekend record among Pixar films,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> among films released in June,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-openingjune_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-openingjune-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> (surpassed by <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)#Box_office" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manofsteel_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-manofsteel-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> and among G-rated films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The film also achieved the second-largest opening weekend for an animated film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> and the fourth-largest opening weekend for a 2010 film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Its average of $27,385 per venue is the second highest for a G-rated film and the second highest for an animated feature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Its opening-week gross (Friday-through-Thursday) of $167.6 million is the largest among animated films, the largest among 2010 films and the 13th largest of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> It also achieved the largest 10-day gross among 2010 films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> It topped the box office for two consecutive weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_North_America">Outside North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Outside North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Toy Story 3</i> is the nineteenth highest-grossing film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overseas_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-overseas-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> the fourth highest-grossing animated film, the third highest-grossing film of 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing Pixar film, and the seventh highest-grossing Disney film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overseas_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-overseas-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> It topped the box office outside North America three times, on its first ($35.0 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> second,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> and sixth weekend (which was its largest).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Its highest-grossing market after North America is Japan ($126.7 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> where it is the second highest-grossing U.S. animated feature (behind <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onebill_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-onebill-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> followed by the U.K. &amp; Ireland and Malta (£73.8 million - $116.6 million), where it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of highest-grossing films in the United Kingdom">fourth highest-grossing film</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> and Mexico ($59.4 million), where it is the second highest-grossing film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mexico_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mexico-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> It set opening weekend records for animated films in Ecuador, Colombia, Mexico, China, Argentina,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Hong Kong,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Spain and the U.K.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the highest-grossing animated film of all time in the U.K., Ireland and Malta,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> in Mexico,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mexico_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mexico-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> in Hong Kong,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> and in Egypt. It is the highest-grossing 2010 film in Argentina,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Bolivia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Chile,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Colombia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Hong Kong,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Mexico,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Spain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> the U.K., Ireland and Malta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On January 25, 2011, the Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences announced that <i>Toy Story 3</i> was not only nominated for Best Animated Feature, but also for Best Picture. This makes <i>Toy Story 3</i> not only the first animated sequel in history to be nominated for Best Picture, but also the third animated film to be nominated for Best Picture (following <i><a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_(1991_film)" title="Beauty and the Beast (1991 film)">Beauty and the Beast</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Up_(2009_film)" title="Up (2009 film)">Up</a></i>), with <i>Toy Story 3</i> becoming the second Pixar film to be nominated for both awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Toy Story 3</i> also became the first ever Pixar film - and the first animated feature film since <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek" title="Shrek">Shrek</a></i> - to be nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Adapted_Screenplay" title="Academy Award for Best Adapted Screenplay">Academy Award for Best Adapted Screenplay</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> though six of Pixar's previous films were nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Screenplay" title="Academy Award for Best Original Screenplay">Best Original Screenplay</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story" title="Toy Story">Toy Story</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATWalleScreenplay_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-LATWalleScreenplay-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATWalleScreenplay_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-LATWalleScreenplay-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Incredibles" title="The Incredibles">The Incredibles</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATWalleScreenplay_131-2"><a href="#cite_note-LATWalleScreenplay-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Ratatouille_(film)" title="Ratatouille (film)">Ratatouille</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATWalleScreenplay_131-3"><a href="#cite_note-LATWalleScreenplay-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/WALL-E" title="WALL-E">WALL-E</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATWalleScreenplay_131-4"><a href="#cite_note-LATWalleScreenplay-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Up_(2009_film)" title="Up (2009 film)">Up</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, it was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="Nickelodeon Kids' Choice Awards">Kids' Choice Award</a> for Favorite Animated Movie, but lost to <i><a href="/wiki/Despicable_Me" title="Despicable Me">Despicable Me</a></i>.</p>

<td>Hollywood Movie Awards 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td>Hollywood Animation Award</td>

</tr>
</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">film score</a> for <i>Toy Story 3</i> was composed and conducted by <a href="/wiki/Randy_Newman" title="Randy Newman">Randy Newman</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BFI_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-BFI-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> his sixth for Pixar after <i>Toy Story</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Bug%27s_Life" title="A Bug's Life">A Bug's Life</a></i>, <i>Toy Story 2</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Monsters,_Inc." title="Monsters, Inc.">Monsters, Inc.</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Cars_(film)" title="Cars (film)">Cars</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> Initially, Disney released the soundtrack only as <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital download</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AboutSoundtrack_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-AboutSoundtrack-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> This was the second instance where Disney did not release the award-winning soundtrack of a Pixar film on CD, the first being <i>Up</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2012, <a href="/wiki/Intrada_Records" title="Intrada Records">Intrada</a> released the <i>Toy Story 3</i> soundtrack on Compact Disc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>All songs written and composed by <a href="/wiki/Randy_Newman" title="Randy Newman">Randy Newman</a>. </p>

<p>In addition to the tracks included in the soundtrack album, the film also uses several other tracks such as "<a href="/wiki/Dream_Weaver" title="Dream Weaver">Dream Weaver</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Wright" title="Gary Wright">Gary Wright</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Le_Freak" title="Le Freak">Le Freak</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Chic_(band)" title="Chic (band)">Chic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iTunesSongbook_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-iTunesSongbook-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> and Randy Newman's original version of "<a href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_a_Friend_in_Me" title="You've Got a Friend in Me">You've Got a Friend in Me</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iTunesSongbook_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-iTunesSongbook-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Furthermore, tracks "Cowboy!" and "Come to Papa" included material from Newman's rejected score to <i><a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One_(film)" title="Air Force One (film)">Air Force One</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Air_Force_One_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Air_Force_One-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> The song "Losing You" from Newman's own album <i><a href="/wiki/Harps_and_Angels" title="Harps and Angels">Harps and Angels</a></i> was also used in the first trailer for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Judas_Priest" title="Judas Priest">Judas Priest</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Electric_Eye_(song)" title="Electric Eye (song)">Electric Eye</a>" was also used in the film in the temp score for the opening scene of <i>Toy Story 3</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> The aliens are playing the tune in their sports car. The song was ultimately replaced by another piece of music.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequel">Sequel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toy_Story_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sequel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span id="Sequels"></span><span id="Sequel"></span><span id="Potential_sequel"></span> Lee Unkrich initially stated that a fourth <i>Toy Story</i> film was not being planned. "Well, we don't have any plans for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toy_Story_4" title="Toy Story 4">Toy Story 4</a></i>," Unkrich said. "I'm flattered that people ask about it—it reminds me how much people love the characters, but it was really important to me with this film that we not just create another sequel, that it not just be another appendage coming off of the other two." Unkrich went on to say, "there may be opportunities for Woody and Buzz in the future, but we don't have any plans for anything right now."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nola-t3_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-nola-t3-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> It has also been reported that Hanks and Allen have signed on for fourth <i>Toy Story</i> film if Pixar ever decides to produce one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheWrap_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheWrap-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> In a BBC interview in 2011, Hanks said that he thought Pixar was working on a sequel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> Disney denied the rumors saying, "nothing is official."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2014, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Iger" title="Bob Iger">Bob Iger</a> confirmed that a fourth <i>Toy Story</i> film would be released in 2017 with <a href="/wiki/John_Lasseter" title="John Lasseter">John Lasseter</a> directing. Lasseter stated "<i>Toy Story 3</i> ended Woody and Buzz's story with Andy so perfectly that for a long time, we never even talked about doing another <i>Toy Story</i> movie. But when Andrew, Pete, Lee and I came up with this new idea, I just could not stop thinking about it. It was so exciting to me, I knew we had to make this movie—and I wanted to direct it myself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">1998–2000</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/A_Bug%27s_Life" title="A Bug's Life">A Bug's Life</a></i> – <a href="/wiki/John_Lasseter" title="John Lasseter">John Lasseter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Stanton" title="Andrew Stanton">Andrew Stanton</a> / <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prince_of_Egypt" title="The Prince of Egypt">The Prince of Egypt</a></i> – <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wells" title="Simon Wells">Simon Wells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brenda_Chapman" title="Brenda Chapman">Brenda Chapman</a>, and Steve Hickner (1998)</li>
